## 1. AI for Blogging： How to Start a Blog and Generate Content Quickly

every day, but when it comes time to
write a blog post about it, you might be
wondering, "Where do I even start?" Not

You've got a discovery call in 20
minutes, three follow-up emails you
haven't written yet, a deal that's been

with no clear next steps, and somewhere

it first.
>>
>> Most reps spend more time hunting for
information than actually
selling. Digging through old emails,
scanning call notes, copy-pasting into
an AI tool hoping it gives you something
useful back. The problem isn't that the
information doesn't exist, it's that
nothing pulls it together for you.
Breeze Assistant does. It's already in
your HubSpot subscription. It already
knows your deals, your contacts, and
your past conversations. And it works
wherever you work. Inside HubSpot on
desktop, in your CRM records, and now
directly inside the HubSpot mobile app.
In this video, I'll walk you through how
a sales rep can use Breeze Assistant to
run a sharper, faster day from morning
prep through post-call follow-up without
switching tabs or starting from scratch.

HubSpot and click the Assistant button
in the top right. It's already there.

switching to email to actually send it.

pricing conversation from last week.

subject, body.
You just hit send. No tab switching, no

## 4. Breeze Customer Agent： Scale Support Using AI

Hey there. Today I'm so excited to show
you how to scale your customer service
efforts using Breeze Customer Agent,
which is available in ServiceHub
Professional and Enterprise. I'm Kyle
and this is how to
HubSpot. The best part about working in
customer service is connecting with
customers and helping them resolve
complex problems they wouldn't be able
to work through on their own. It's
incredibly rewarding. But the reality is
there are always a lot of routine tasks
and questions that need to be resolved
and that can be really tedious. That's
where Breeze customer agent comes in.
It's like having a super dedicated
teammate who's always available any hour
of the day to respond to these routine
inquiries so you can focus on working
through the more complicated questions.
In this video, I'll show you how Breeze
Customer Agent can transform your
support experience. From quick setup and
personalized customer interactions to
the impressive 60% resolution rate, your
team will be freed up for highv value
work. Getting started with Breeze
customer agent is surprisingly simple.
Most customers can have it up and
running in just 15 minutes. Let's walk
through it together. To set up your
customer agent, first you're going to
need to navigate to this page, which is
under the breeze menu in the main
navigation. And here you can set up the
basic aspects of your agent. You can
give it a name. You can select its role.
For this example, we'll use customer
support. You can even select a kind of
personality. Choose the one that best
matches your business. For this example,
we'll use friendly. Once you've done
that, come to the content tab to choose
what information this agent will have
access to as it's answering customer
inquiries. You can upload files such as
PDFs and text files, or you can choose
HubSpot content to train this agent on.
You can even import public URLs from any
website, and these will be automatically
updated once a week. And now your
customer agent is trained and ready to
respond to customer inquiries. But
before you turn it on, let me show you a
few customization options. First, let's
talk about how your agent hands off
conversations. What I mean by that is if
an urgent or sensitive matter comes
through that your agent can't resolve,
you want as smooth of a process as
possible for them to be able to escalate
that to a team member. And whether your
team is currently available or they're
offline at max capacity or out of
office, you can customize the language
the agent will use to make it as clear
as possible to your customers what to
expect next. To customize your handoffs,
come back to the configuration tab and
this time select the handoff option. On
this screen, you can customize all of
your availability messaging. So if the
team is available, the customer agent
will use this language. If the team is
at max capacity, it'll send this message
here. If the team is away or outside of
their working hours or a handoff is
otherwise unavailable, you can customize
the exact words the agent will use in
talking to your customers. Down here at
the bottom, you can set specific
keywords or phrases that will trigger an
automatic handoff. So, if someone wants
to discuss something sensitive like
pricing or cancel my subscription or if
they have, for example, a billing
question, you can set up these keywords
and the agent will always hand off these
conversations to an available team
member. Now that handoffs are in place,
it's time to assign Breeze customer
agent to your customer support channels
and decide who it will hand off to when
it can't answer a question. To set this
up, come to the assignment tab and then
click this assign button. Here you see
all your available channels for this
agent to operate in. Live chat,
WhatsApp, Facebook Messenger, calling,
and email. For this example, let's
choose live chat and then click next.
Here are the available live chats in
this account. We'll have our agent
working in this one. Click next. And now
you decide what happens when it's time
for a handoff. Whether you want the
agent to hand off to a human agent or
you want it to stay assigned. If you do
want to hand off to a human agent, you
can select which specific users and
teams it will hand off to. And if no
human agent is available, you can decide
whether your customer agent will stay
assigned or leave the conversation. Once
you've selected all your options, click
assign. and your agent is now working.
With your Breeze agent assigned to the
right channels, you're now ready to
engage with your customers at scale. All
right, we've now set up the basics of a
Breeze customer agent. Now, let's go a
level deeper and look at some advanced
use cases. In addition to everything
we've looked at so far, your customer
agent can also access customer specific
information in any of your applications.
So, it can answer questions like, "What
is the status of my order?" or take
simple actions like resetting a
password. These kinds of queries make up
up to 50% of customer support volume.
And the best part, these new
capabilities will free up your support
team for more strategic work. To set up
this kind of action, come to the actions
tab. Here you can see a couple of
actions I've already set up in this
account. One is order status, which has
been published, and the other is
password reset, which is currently a
draft. Let's edit password reset so you
can see what these actions look like. Up
at the top, you'll give your action a
name and a description. And then you'll
select trigger phrases. If one of your
customers says this trigger phrase to
your customer agent, it will know it's
time to start this action. Below that,
you define required inputs. So, if
you're looking up someone's password,
you'll need to know their email address
associated with their account. And you
can set that up so it gets collected
here. Next is this configure API
section. If your customer agent is going
to use this action to pull information
from an external system, you'll want one
of the engineers who built that system
to fill in this next part. The last
section is response instructions, where
you'll tell the agent what to do after
the action is complete. Once you've got
this set up, you can come to this
preview tab to see what the action will
look like in real life. So, if someone
says, in this example, I'm locked out,
the agent will respond by asking them
for their email address so it can send a
password reset email. When you're happy
with the way it's set up, come up to the
publish button and turn it on. And just
like that, Breeze customer agent is set
up to maximize your team's productivity.
If you're running a business, there's
one thing that matters more than
anything else. Outcomes. Yes, this agent
can do all kinds of incredible things,
but how do you know it's actually
delivering results for your business?
Let's take a look at the metrics that
matter. To see reports about your
customer agent, come to this performance
tab. And right here at the top, you'll
see the impact this agent is having this
week. You can see how many conversations
it resolved, handled, its time to
resolution, and its visitor feedback.

## 6. Customer Agent： Deploy with confidence and optimize as you scale

Your support team is stretched thin.
Customers expect instant answers.
Tickets pile up faster than you can
respond. Sound familiar? Customer Agent
handles routine inquiries 24/7, freeing
your team to focus on complex issues
that require judgment, empathy, and
expertise. Since launch, you've told us
what needs improvement, and we listened.
In this video, I'll show you safer ways
to get started, better control over your
rollout, tools to build confidence
before going live, and clearer
visibility into what's working. I'm
Kyle, and this is how to
HubSpot.
Let's start with the easiest way to get

risk-f free. If you're on HubSpot Pro or
higher and haven't started using
Customer Agent yet, you can try it for 4
weeks without using any credits. That's

actual support traffic and see exactly
how it performs. To get started,
navigate to ServiceHub in your HubSpot
account. Click on customer agent in the
sidebar. Click set up your agent to
start the free trial. Follow the setup
wizard to connect your channels. We
recommend support teams connect channels
to the help desk workspace. Customers
using help desk and customer agent see
better outcomes in terms of ticket
response and resolution. It's required
if you want to use the email channel and
reply recommendations. The help desk is
designed for humans and customer agent
to work together and there are handoff
reports, specific views and more to
ensure seamless collaboration. This
gives you real time to evaluate how
customer agent handles your specific use
case before committing any credits. No

results with your real support volume.
Now that you're testing, let's talk

has been your number one request since
launch, and we've delivered. Agent
guidelines give you granular control
over exactly how the agent communicates
with your customers. Here's how to set

guidelines in the left sidebar. Under
tone, you'll see a text box where you
can write detailed instructions.
Tell the agent how to talk, formal or
casual, warm or professional, detailed
or concise.
Add specific phrases to use or avoid.
Then click test draft. For example, you
could write, "Use a warm, confident
tone. Address customers by name. Never
sound rushed. For technical terms,
explain briefly. If you're unsure,
acknowledge it and offer to connect them
with a human. If your brand is formal,
make it formal. If you're casual and
friendly, make it casual. The agent will
follow your lead. Email and chat are
different animals. What works in a quick
chat message doesn't always work in
email. With channel settings, you can
customize how the agent behaves in each
channel. To configure channel specific
behavior, go to channel settings in the
left sidebar.
Select email or messaging. For messaging

settings, and test again. You'll see

interpreted the questions, and what it
recommended. No more blind deployments.

experience. Here's a feature that saves

blasts that somehow ended up in your

wasting credits on conversations that go

Add email addresses or domains you want

messages, spam. Add them to the ignore

## 7. Data Enrichment and Buyer Intent： More context for better outcomes

Your CRM is only as powerful as the data
that powers it. Blank fields mean missed
opportunities. Incomplete records mean
guesswork instead of real-time insights.
Outdated information means wasted
outreach. Data enrichment automatically
fills in the gaps of your missing data
with details like job titles, company
specifics, and technologies used so you
can segment better, personalize smarter,
and close faster. We've been focused on
making enrichment more comprehensive,
more transparent, and more trustworthy.
These updates give you richer contact
and company data with the control and
visibility you need to confidently scale
enrichment across your business. In this
video, I'll show you how to get more
complete data, plus the transparency and
control you can trust. I'm Kyle and this
is how to HubSpot.
Let me show you how we've expanded our
data coverage and improved quality
across the board. We've added new data
sources to fill gaps in contact records,
particularly for EU based businesses.
Here's what's improved. Job titles are
now more frequently populated. Company
details are more accurate and location
information is more complete. This helps
you segment audiences more effectively
and personalize outreach with confidence
when working with European contacts or
companies. Let's see enrichment in
action. Navigate to contacts in your
HubSpot CRM.
Open a contact record with incomplete
information.
Look for the enrichment panel on the
right side.
Click enrich contact.
Watch as missing fields populate
automatically. You'll see job titles,
company information, social profiles,
and more appear in seconds. Here's a big
improvement. We used to skip enriching a
contact if we only had limited
information. That meant you missed out
on potential data for new or incomplete
records in your CRM. Now, enrichment
works even when data is limited. For
example, we can infer a name from an
email address. We can find a company
from a domain. We can fill in location
data from partial information. You get
immediate value from every enriched
record. Even if you're starting with
just an email address, we've expanded
our data sources to surface 10% more
legitimate company news and activity
signals. This means more actionable
intelligence flowing into your workflows
about the current state of a company,
more opportunities to spot high intent
prospects based on recent news, and more
relevant conversation starters for your
reps. For example, if a prospect's
company just announced a funding round,
acquired another business, or launched a
new product, you'll know about it.
That's powerful context for outreach and
conversation. To see these and other
intent signals, let's open a company
record in your CRM.
Scroll to the enrichment section.
Look for company news and intent
signals.
You'll see recent announcements, funding
events, hiring trends, and other buying
signals. Your reps can use this
intelligence to personalize pitches and
time their outreach better. The number
one barrier to enrichment adoption is
fear. Fear that it'll overwrite
carefully managed data, that data will
come from unknown sources, or that
you'll have limited control over what
happens. Let me show you how we've
addressed every one of those concerns.
You now have complete control over how
enriched data populates your CRM
records. Here's how to configure it. Go
to settings
and in the data management section,
click on data enrichment.
Click on the mapping tab and here you
see all the properties that get
enriched. For each one, you can choose
whether you want to fill empty values
only, fill empty values, and overwrite
existing values, or not fill any values.
You can also choose to match an
enrichment property to any HubSpot
property. For example, let's say you
have a custom property called job
function that you've carefully
segmented. You don't want enrichment to
overwrite any previously recorded data
there. Set that property to fill empty
fields only. Or maybe you have a last
enrichment date field that you always
want to update. Set that to always
overwrite. You can also map enriched
data to completely different properties.
Map enriched job title to your custom RO
property. Map enriched company size to
your custom employee range field. Map
enriched industry to your custom
vertical property. This flexibility
removes the fear that enrichment might
corrupt your data. You're in complete
control. Let me walk you through how to
set up enrichment for the first time.
Step one, enable enrichment. Go to
settings, data management,
enrichment. Choose which type of records
to enrich: contacts, companies, or both.
Step two, configure property mapping.
Click property mapping. For each
enriched property, choose your behavior.
Fill empty values only is the safest
option. Fill empty values and overwrite
existing values for properties you want
kept fresh. Do not fill any values for
properties you don't want enriched at
all. Step three, choose your enrichment
method. You have three options.
Automatic enrichment enriches records
automatically as they enter your
database from form submissions, imports,
or integrations. In enrichment settings,
toggle on automatic enrichment. You can
do this separately for companies and
contacts for when new records are
created and to continuously enrich
existing records. Manual enrichment
enriches individual records with a
single click when you need fresh data.
To see this in action, go to the
contacts page, open any contact or
company record that's missing data. Find
the actions dropdown in the lefth hand
panel and click enrich record. HubSpot
will display the available properties
which you can check and uncheck. And
when you're ready, click enrich record
and batch enrichment fills data gaps at
scale across entire segments. Create a
segment or select existing contacts.
Click more and then enrich records and
then confirm the enrichment. You can use
all three methods together. Automatic
enrichment handles incoming records.
Manual enrichment gives you ondemand
control and batch enrichment fills
historical gaps. Data enrichment is
included with HubSpot's smart CRM and
works seamlessly across the platform.
More complete data means better
segmentation. Better segmentation means
smarter targeting. Smarter targeting
means higher conversions and enrichment
handles it all automatically. If you

## 8. How to Build a Consistent Sales Process

Every sales team I talk to always has
that one system or process that they say
is their single source of truth, but it
never quite matches what's in their CRM.
Sound familiar? Think about your current
sales process for just a minute here.
You know that one rep who always has
this really specific way of qualifying
leads. Then of course you have people
that will say there is only one way to
send proposals. And when it comes to
forecasting, well, let's just say
there's a whole lot of guesswork
involved. Not only is this causing
headaches with managers and leaders, but
it's making it really difficult to track
accurate data and have accurate
processes for your teams to follow. But
don't worry, I'm going to show you how
to bring some consistency to your sales
processes without making things feel too
rigid or too bureaucratic. We'll cover
customizing your pipeline, setting up
smart automations, and creating
playbooks your teams will actually use.

HubSpot. By the way, you can follow

## 14. How to Generate AI Images For Your Website That Actually Look Good

You've probably seen AI generated images
that are weird, distressing, or just
plain bad. But most of this comes down
to understanding where AI's strengths
and weaknesses lie in image generation.
If you have Content Hub, you can use AI
to generate images for all of your
content inside HubSpot. I'm Kyle and
this is How to HubSpot. Let's take a
look at how you can use HubSpot to
generate images that'll work for you. If
you'd like to follow along, click the
link in the description below. Let's get
started.
I just finished writing a blog post.
I've got to publish it in about 10
minutes. The last thing I need to do is
find a stock image to go on it to add
some impact. The blog post is about
collaboration. So, I'm just going to
search my favorite sock image site for
that.
And I don't really know what this image
has to do with collaboration. If this
story sounds familiar to you, you could
benefit from using AI image generation
inside HubSpot. Let me show you how to
do it. Good images make your content
more engaging and interesting. But
finding the right image for your
particular piece of content can
sometimes be a challenge. There are so
many different websites offering stock
images, it can be overwhelming. And on
top of that, finding an image that
exactly matches your particular piece of
content can be really hard. This is
where AI is making a big difference.
With AI image generation, you don't
search for an existing image, you create
a new one for your content. For this
example, let's generate some images for
a blog post. Here I am on the blog post
page inside HubSpot which is under
content blog and I can choose a blog
post that I've already created and that
will bring me into the blog post editor
and I'm going to add an image right here
in the body of it. So I'll click the
image button here. If you have images in
your files you can select them or you
can generate with AI. You have three
options here when you're generating an
image in HubSpot. You're going to
describe the image you want. You can
choose a specific style or let the AI
decide it. And you can choose what
dimensions you want. square, landscape,
or portrait. For this example, we'll
stick with square and style decided by
AI. And the thing that's really great
about AI image generation is that the
sky is the limit. Literally anything you
can think of, you can generate an image
for using AI. So, for this example,
let's generate a space cowboy on Jupiter
wrangling Martian ducks. All right, not
too bad, AI. I kind of like this one.
Uh, but you'll notice, you know, his
feet are sort of in weird spots. We've
got a bit of extra clothing over here.
The fact of the matter is, the more
elements you ask for in your image, the
more things can go wrong. In general,
it's best to keep your prompts specific
but simple. So, if we limit this to just
space cowboy, we'll hopefully get
something a little better. I could
probably make use of one of these, but
the point is simpler is usually better.
And on the topic of simplicity, it's
better to have concrete prompts than
abstract ones. Let me show you what I
mean. If I ask for something really
concrete like a grocery store, I'll
usually get an image that's pretty good.
Those look like grocery stores. But if I
ask for something completely abstract,
like synergy, it's anyone's guess what I
might get. These images are fine, I
guess, but it's hard to say whether
they're really encapsulating synergy.
So, keep things simple and concrete, and
you'll usually get better results. One
thing you should play around with as
you're generating these images is the
different styles that are available to
you. Take a look at this. If I want to
create an image of construction
vehicles, I can let the AI decide the
style or I can take a more hands-on
approach and say maybe I want a photo
realalistic image. Now, you have to be
careful with photorealistic images. As
you can see, this is not a real
construction vehicle. So, a lot of times
it'll be better to choose a more
stylistic option. For example, one I
really like inside of HubSpot is
origami. If we generate origami versions
of construction vehicles, any errors or
if they aren't quite to scale, we'll
just make them simply more adorable. I
really like these little guys. Let's try
another option. How about anime? We'll
generate using the exact same prompt.
And these images look like they may have
come from an anime cartoon. The point
is, there are a lot of different styles
you can use when you're generating
images to make sure they match the tone
and feel of your website. And that's AI
powered image generation inside HubSpot.
Remember, less is more. Concrete is
better than abstract. And be sure to
give different styles a try so the
images can match the look and feel of
your website and brand. If you'd like to
try it for yourself, click the link in
the description below. I'm Kyle and this
is How to HubSpot. See you next time.

## 15. How to Keep AI True to Your Brand Voice

Establishing a brand voice for your
business is one of the most important
things that you could do. It's also one
of the hardest. And I should know
because I've experienced those
challenges so many times in the past. I
have a social media marketing agency and
the type of client that I want to
attract are those that want to create
bold, impactful, fun content. So, I've
always known that I needed to create a
tone of voice that reflected that. But
not only is it difficult to define a
tone of voice that truly reflects your
brand, but it's even harder to ensure
that it's consistent across all of your
content. From emails to ads to blog
posts to website copy, it starts
sounding all over the place very
quickly. That's why I'm going to show
you a tool that's made this whole
process so much easier. It's helped me
create a brand voice I am truly proud
of. Follow along with me by clicking the
link in the description below. Let's get
into it.
To set up your brand voice, head into
your HubSpot settings. Click on
accounts, then defaults, and you'll see
an option called brand voice. Click on
generate brand voice. This will open up
a window where you can add a writing
example and give some context about your
brand. So, basically, here's what it
says. The writing example that you're
going to send is going to be analyzed
and used to generate your brand voice.
So full samples that are longer than 500
words do the best job at accurately
representing your brand voice and it's
usually going to yield the best results.
I'm choosing to paste a writing sample.
For me, I do believe that my best
examples of my writing are from my email
newsletters. I have an email series
called A Letter to My Readers. It's a
monthly series where I show the behind
the scenes of running a business, the
raw, messy middle. Because it's so raw,
it really demonstrates my authentic tone
of voice. So, it's the perfect right
example to develop my brand voice. So,
I'm going to copy one of these
newsletters and then paste it in. Select
a target audience for this sample. So,
I'm going to write content creators
and business owners.
And that's in. So, now HubSpot can
generate my brand voice. Now, this is
the interesting part. HubSpot's going to
pick up on the characteristics within
your writing and it's actually going to
tell you what your brand voice is. One
of my favorite parts about this is that
it's not just going to lock you into
whatever it says. You're actually able
to jump in and make some adjustments to
make sure it truly aligns with what you
feel your brand voice should be. So, as
you can see, mine says that the
personality is authentic, human, and
supportive. And then it breaks down the
tone as reflective and conversational,
which I think is spoton. That's exactly
the vibe I'm going for. I would say
though, there's probably a few elements
that I might want to throw in there. So,
I want to make sure that there's some
sarcasm and some witty to really lighten
the tone of my content. Otherwise, I
think it'd sound a little bit too
intense. So, I'm going to just pop that
in.
I'm also going to add down to earth. And
the reason why is because since the
beginning stages of my career, I have
always tried to sound like your mate who
works in marketing who's just here to
help. So, I think adding down to earth
is going to really help me convey that.
So, in the advanced settings, you can
also add your company's mission and even
include some terms to avoid, which is
very, very useful. So, my company's
mission is helping bold brands turn
cultural insight
into social media content that actually
works.
There's also a section on inclusivity,
which I think is so important. I'm going
to choose to use genderneutral nouns and
pronouns. I also really enjoy using
slang and idioms. I feel like it just
adds a bit of character to my content.
So, I'm going to leave those in, but I
am going to select to avoid cultural and
religious references. Once that's all
done, I'm going to hit save. And there
you have it. Your brand voice is set up.
Now, this is where it gets really
clever. You can choose which channels
you want your brand voice to show up in.
And that choice really matters.
Personally, I wouldn't want to use my
full tone of voice in something like a
case study. These should be clear,
concise, and really easy to understand,
so there's no need to be throwing in my
sarcasm or witty oneliners. I actually
spend a lot of time thinking about where
my tone of voice should be applied. As
much as I would love for it to show up
everywhere, there really is a time and a
place for my tone of voice. It's
important to use that kind of tone
intentionally. So, for example, in case
studies, clarity is really the goal.
People should be able to quickly
understand the results without being
distracted by personalitydriven copy.
Plus, I'm usually talking about someone
else's brand and their success. So, I
keep the tone more neutral out of
respect. It's about their story, not
mine. But you can see here that there is
an option to select blog posts, emails,
website pages, podcast content, social
media. That's where I want my full tone
of voice to really shine. So, I'm going
to select those and click save. Now,
let's see it all in action. Let's go
into one of the website pages that I set
up earlier so that we can see this in
action. So, I'm clicking on a section of
text on my homepage. I'm going to double
click it so I can open up the editor and
find that trusty refine tool. There it
is. Let's click on it and select apply
brand identity. So, the co-pilot is
going to pop up and it's going to
rewrite that text for you in line with
your brand identity. So, as you can see,
it's reddrafted this text to make it a
lot more witty, more conversational, a
bit more down to earth, and I think it's
sounding pretty good. I'd even go so far
to say that the phrasing, the rhythm,
and the energy of this piece of content
is pretty spot-on. However, ever the
perfectionist, I do want to make a small
tweak just to improve it further. So,
any tweaks that you want to make to the
copy, you can just write it in here. I'm
just going to ask it to remove the
dashes. And then a few seconds later,
you've got the updated copy without the
dash. It sounds like me. It sounds like
my brand. And it's good to go. So now
I'm going to go through all of the rest
of my homepage and basically just do the
same thing. It literally takes seconds
and it will allow me to update all of
the content to ensure the tone is super
consistent. Also, the messaging will
feel really clear and aligned with my
brand. This tool is a game changer if
you work with a team. I've recently
started building out my own team, and

across is tone consistency. Even if
someone understands my brand voice, they
still might interpret it slightly
differently, which means you end up with
content that kind of sounds like me but
not really, or it sounds like me in some
places but not everywhere. Now, this
fixes those inconsistencies. It gives
the whole team the same guide, the same
language, the same tone. So whether it's
someone writing an email, a blog post,

aligned. You're not stuck reworking
everyone's writing or playing editor on

## 22. How to Score and Prioritize Leads Like a Pro with HubSpot

Are you struggling to figure out which
leads to focus on and how to convert
them faster? Hi, I'm Angel. I'm a
marketing specialist working in tech. In
this video, I'm going to show you how to
master lead scoring and prioritization
within HubSpot. We're going to go over
how to set up smart and effective
scoring rules and then how to integrate
those scores into your marketing
strategy. If you want to follow along,
you can use the link in the description
to get HubSpot for free. This is how to
HubSpot.
Lead scoring may sound complicated, but
it's essentially a system that allows
sales and marketing to prioritize their
leads based on their potential to
convert. It's like a shortcut to
identify who you should be talking to
first. Lead scoring will assign a
numerical value to your lead as well as
a low, medium, or hot label based on
that value. The score is evaluated based
on multiple factors such as how they
interacted with your site, their
demographic information, their
professional details, and even all the
ways that you have interacted with them,
like through ads or emails or SMS. The
higher the score, the warmer the lead,
meaning they're more likely to be
interested in your product or service.
Lead scoring can be a really, really
important tool for sales and marketing
teams because it helps those teams
prioritize their time and ensure that
they're focusing on the warmest leads
first. So, how do we set up lead scoring
within HubSpot? Let's dive in. To start,
we have to head over to the marketing
tab and then down to lead scoring. Now,
you can either create your new score
with AI or do it all on your own. Let's
try it with AI first. First, we select
what kind of score you want to create.
So, is it a contact engagement score or
is it a contact fit score? A contact
engagement score measures your contact's
level of engagement based on their
behaviors and interactions. And then a
contact fit score evaluates how closely
that contact aligns with your ideal
customer based on their demographics and
other criteria. Let's go ahead and
select contact engagement score. First,
we want to give our score a name. So,
I'm just going to call it May engagement
score. Then, we want to fill out the
fields below. So, there is your start
stage and I want to leave that as lead.
And then in the successful end stages, I
want to also add marketing qualified
leads as well as the sales qualified
lead. For the time frame, we're going to
select 90 days. Once you hit create
score, HubSpot will start to evaluate
all of your contacts based on that
score. It really is that easy to do it
with AI. If you want to create a score
on your own, you'll have to add in the
events and property rules yourself. So
again, we're going to choose whether we
want contact engagement, contact fit, or
a combined score. We're going to do
combine score. So for example, let's say
we want to add in the event of a page
visit. So we'll add an event group.
We'll hit add event criteria and then
scroll down to web events. Then when you
hit select event, you'll be able to see
page visited. So from there you can add
in more detail. So you can filter the
event by URL or by browser or by city.
You can also add in an additional time
frame as well. So, in the last 90 days
or 30 days or 60 days or whatever you
like. And then you'll have to decide how
many points that event adds. So, let's
do 10 points. If you want to add in
multiple scoring groups, you can do that
as well. So, let's say you want one for
awareness and one for conversion. So, to
do that, we can just go down to add
event group and then it'll create a new
scoring group for you. So if this
scoring group is more for awareness
and the second scoring group is more for
conversions, then we might want to
adjust the weight of each scoring group.
So right now we have the first one set
to 100. So since it's for awareness,
maybe let's set this to 30. For my
conversion group, I'm going to add in
something like a form entry because that
shows me that the lead is more
interested. To personalize your lead
even further, you can actually add in a
DK score, but you can't do it if you
have a time frame. So, let's turn off
our time frame and then turn on DK
scores. Then you can choose how much you
want to reduce the score by and how
often. So, let's say we're going to
reduce it by 30% every 3 months. This
way, you'll have a more accurate photo
of exactly how warm those leads really
are. Once you're happy with your scoring
groups, we can head over to the contacts
tab and select what groups of contacts
we want this score to apply to. So, we
can do it for all of our contacts or
specific lists that you may have. In the
settings tab, you'll be able to label
your new score value. So, we'll call
this May combined score. And voila, you
can go ahead and review and turn on your
score. If you want to set up an
automation that is based on your new
lead score, for example, once one of
your leads hits 100 points, we can do
that under automation and workflows.
When we go into create workflow, we'll
be able to decide what action triggers
this workflow. To find your new lead
score, we can go into data changes and
then record meets a set of custom filter
conditions. Then we can select contact
and then select contact properties. In
here, you'll be able to find the lead
score that you just created and name.
So, mine was called combined score. So,
in here, we're just going to type in is
equal to 100 points. And then voila,
this workflow is going to be triggered
once one of your leads hits 100 points
based on your new criteria. Since we
know this lead is quite warm and quite
active, we can do something like sending
out an email as the action with maybe a
special offer because we know they're
more likely to convert. Other ways that
I would recommend you using your lead
scores are to prioritize follow-ups to
those warm leads, to segment based on
your lead scores within your marketing
campaigns, to create an automated lead
nurturing campaign for those people who
have lower scores. You can even use your
lead scores as a benchmark for your
campaigns to see how a campaign has
performed based on how engaged a
customer is. And there you have it.
That's how you can use HubSpot's
powerful lead scoring and automation
features to really streamline your sales
process and enhance your marketing
strategies. By having these systems in
place, you're really making sure that no
lead gets left behind and that your team
can focus on the most promising
prospects. My very last tip is to
revisit your automations and your
criteria often. You want to make sure
that they are aligned with your
marketing and your sales goals.
HubSpot's features are designed to be
flexible so that they can actually grow
with you while you grow. If you found
this tutorial helpful, definitely check
out the other videos on this channel.
Also, if you want to try out any of
these features, you can try HubSpot for
free through the link in the
description. I'm Angel and I'll catch
you in the next one.

What is a smart CRM? Well, all a smart
CRM is is an AI powered platform that's
going to consolidate all of your data
into one place. So, the idea behind a
CRM is that it's one platform. And when
I say platform, I mean it's going to
tell your whole business story. So,
contacts, conversations, deals, support
tickets, I can see it all in one place.
I can see all the information that I
need. And then once I have that
information in HubSpot, I'm going to get
connected data. So I'm going to connect
my email. I'm going to connect my
website. So then I'll be able to see
what are my contacts and companies up
to. I can get a timeline of their
activity. And what happens is once your
CRM has all this data, it's going to get
smarter over time because you can use AI
automation and reporting that's going to
have access to all this information all
in one place. So, the idea is I can
click on to my a lead that I'm working.
I can see all the information about
them, the company they work for, what
they've been up to, and I can use AI to
ask to tell me what's the next step,
where do I go from here? Write me a
follow-up email. It's all in one place
for you. So, how does HubSpot
specifically store all of this data?
Well, HubSpot uses a data model. And all
a data model is is a visual
representation of an organization's
data. So, how do you store your
different elements and how do they
relate between each other? So, with
HubSpot's data model, you have your
contacts, your companies, your deals,
and your tickets. These are objects in
HubSpot, not an object like my coffee,
right? When I say an object, what I mean
is that this individual piece of data
has its own record. So if I'm storing a
contact, I can click on the contact and
it's going to open up its own record
where I can see all the information
about the contact. So the contact
represents any person that interacts
with your business or your team. And
then companies are going to represent
the organizations that we work for that
they work for. So I click on a contact
record, I can see, oh, Ashley works for
HubSpot. I can see that all in one
place. Deals represent those revenue
opportunities. So I can see if there's
any current opportunities and tickets
represent are there any you know current
customer issues are there any post sales
processes going on. So each of these are
its own object they have their own
record with information but they all
connect with each other. If you have
enterprise you can also always create
any custom objects. So that's how we
store data from a bird's eye view. And
then within each record, so within the
contact record itself, within the
company record itself, we have
properties and properties represent
fields of information. So if I click
into my own contact record, I click into
Ashley's contact record, I can see that
Ashley works for HubSpot, but I also
want to see information about this
contact like first name, email address,
phone number, life cycle stage. So we
call those properties. So, all
properties are in HubSpot are fields of
information that we need to use so that
we can put in the info that we need
about our contacts or companies. Luckily
for us all, we all already have a
library of default properties in
HubSpot. They're already there. They're
ready to go. Like, of course, street
address, phone number, email address.
But then, of course, you know, we're not
only coming from different places in the
world. We're coming from different
industries, right? So, we're going to
need to create our custom properties. So
custom properties represent information
that you need to store that's unique to
your business. So think about if you
have a spreadsheet of contacts, what's
some information you're storing about
them? Some of that some of those fields,
they might not exist in HubSpot. So we
have to create them. Common ones we see
are customer tier, client type, referral
source, product of interest, and then
you might have some that are more unique
to your business. for example, and pause
for wellness. I need to know what pet
size the lead is looking for so that I
don't show up to the office with a great
DNE when they're expecting a Chihuahua.
Right? So, we want to make sure we have
those custom fields in HubSpot ready to
go so that we can store the right
information.

make sure that they have the right seats

you add a user into your HubSpot
account, you need to make sure that they
have a seat and that they have
permissions. The seat is the baseline
access of tools. So seat is like you
have a bucket of tools. You give a user
you you're you give a user a seat and
you say here here's the bucket of tools
that you can have. It gives them the
initial access of the tools. That's the
seat. And then permissions is where you
come in and say you can't do this and
you can do that. So permissions is a
little bit more specific where you're
telling a user specifically what they
have access to in the account. There are
different types of seats in HubSpot and
they're each tiered. The view only seat
is the lowest level of access. It just
means they can view the data but they
can't actually edit or manage anything
in the CRM. So a view only seat's really
only for executives, board members,
stakeholders. Think upper management,
they might need a view only seat. The
core seat is a default for most of the
team. So if you're not sure what seat to
give a user, you could always start with
the core seat and you could upgrade. And
the core seat gives users access to all
the marketing and the operations tools.
So think creating marketing campaigns,
designing emails, operations. That would
be the core seat. And then we have one
level up from the core seat. That's the
sales or the service seat. So the sales
or the service seat gives you the
highest level access. So it gives you
the core seat plus more and it gives you
dedicated workspaces to manage your
leads and manage your customers. So the
sales of the service seat is for folks
that are going to be communicating
directly with leads or directly with
customers. Natasha said, "Wouldn't

## 30. HubSpot Prospecting Agent： Build Pipeline with AI (6 min)

Your reps spend half their day
researching accounts. By the time they
figure out who to email, the momentum's
gone. The other half goes to outreach
that still gets ignored because every
other rep is sending the same templated
message to the same buyer.
Personalization breaks the moment you
try to scale it. And the data your team
needs to do this well, the call notes,
the past conversations, the engagement
signals, is all sitting in your CRM
untouched. Prospecting Agent fixes all
of that. It monitors your market for
buying signals, sources contacts at the
accounts that are ready to buy now, and
writes personalized outreach grounded in
real research and your CRM history. Reps
can review and approve before anything
sends, or you can let the agent run. So,
you keep the quality and they keep their
time. We've heard a lot from customers
since this launched. What you're getting
now is the agent we built in response.
Sharper research, more flexible
configuration, multi-channel outreach,
and a direct line into the workflows you
already run. In this video, I'll show
you how to run signal-based outbound
end-to-end. How the agent prioritizes
accounts, how it researches and drafts
outreach, how to configure your strategy
with plays, how to control the messaging
and the brand voice, and how to scale
into automation when you're ready.
>>
>> I'm Kyle, and this is how to HubSpot.
>>
>> Most outbound starts with a list. Names
you bought, accounts your team picked,
contacts who opened an email once. The
problem isn't the list,
>>
>> it's that nothing on it tells you who's
ready to talk to you right now.
Prospecting Agent watches your market
for that signal. From the overview page,
the agent shows you a daily queue of
monitored companies prioritized by
what's actually changed in each one.
Funding rounds, hiring spikes, product
launches, technology adoption, recent
engagement. For every company, it tells
you why now, the specific signal that
triggered the recommendation. This is
the shift. Your reps stop guessing which
accounts to prioritize. They walk into
their day with a list the agent has
already prioritized for them with the
reasoning attached. Click into any
company in your queue and you'll see the
agent has already done the work most
reps spend hours on. On the left,
recommended contacts. These can come
from your CRM and from connected
providers like ZoomInfo, Apollo, or Surf
if you have them integrated. So, your
reps aren't limited to contacts you
already have. Each contact comes with a
why this contact explanation. Why this
person at this company at this moment.
Grounded in their role, the company's
situation, and the signal the agent
surfaced. In the center, a drafted
outreach email. Personalized, specific,
not a token swap with a name and a
company name.
The agent pulled in recent company news,
layered in CRM contacts from past
conversations, and used the signal to
shape what it said. If you want to see
the work behind the draft, click view
more. You'll see the actual research the
agent ran. Recent news, key updates, a
company summary. Your reps can verify
before they ever send. And anything they
want to refine, they can edit directly
or pass to Breeze assistant for a
rewrite. So, how does the agent know
what to look for, who to reach, and what
to say? That all lives in something we
call a play. A play is the blueprint the
agent runs continuously. You can define
it once, the agent executes against it
every day. Open any play and you'll see
five tabs. The first two define the
strategy. In audience, you tell the
agent who to focus on. The target
companies, the buying signals you care
about, the personas that matter, and how
many contacts to surface each day. So,
instead of your team guessing when to
reach out, the agent watches for those
moments automatically. In selling
context, the agent reads your website
and builds a working understanding of
what you sell, the problems you solve,
and your value proposition. You can edit
any of it. This is where the quality of
the outreach comes from because the
agent isn't writing from a generic
prompt. It's writing from your business.
Audience and selling context tell the
agent what it's working with. The next
two tabs control how the outreach
actually goes out. In the outreach tab,
you choose how the agent runs. Adaptive
mode is the more hands-off option. The
agent decides timing and messaging in
real time based on what each prospect is
doing. You can guide it with advanced
instructions, tone, focus areas, or
rules to follow. Switch to sequence mode
if you want more structure. Multi-step,
multi-channel, AI drafted emails, call
tasks, LinkedIn actions, all in the same
flow.
Within each email, the agent uses smart
blocks. The conversation starter, the
value proposition, the call to action
are each in their own AI-powered block.
You can give each one its own custom
instruction. So, you're not just
generating an email, you're guiding how
each part of the message gets written.
Now switch to guardrails. This is where
your brand stays intact. Choose who the
email is sent from, the contact owner, a
specific rep, or a shared inbox. Set the
tone of voice, configure the language,
define the call to action, whether
that's booking a meeting, sharing a doc,
or pointing to a specific resource. The
agent does the writing, you are still in
control. The last tab is automation.
This is where you decide how hands-on or
hands-off you want to be. Most teams
start in review mode. Every email the
agent drafts comes to a rep first. They
approve, edit, or skip. That's how our
teams build trust in the quality. As
confidence grows, you move toward more
autonomy. The agent sends without
review. It still pulls back when
prospects engage, reply, or book a
meeting, so you never over message. You
don't have to choose one and stick with
it. Different plays can run at different
autonomy levels. Adaptive sends for
lower priority segments, review first
for your most important accounts.
When you head back to the overview,
you'll see the impact in real time.
Companies monitored, contacts engaged,
replies, meetings booked, and which
plays are pulling the most weight. So,
you can measure what's actually
generating pipeline, not just what looks
busy. That's how Prospecting Agent works
end-to-end. The Agent finds the right
accounts at the right time. It
researches and drafts personalized
outreach. You define the strategy with
plays. You control the brand and the
messaging. You scale into automation at
your pace. If you're using HubSpot,
Prospecting Agent lives in the Sales
workspace and is now available at the
Starter tier. Open it, set up your first
play, and start watching the queue.
Thanks for watching. I'm Kyle.
This is How to HubSpot, and I'll catch
you in the next one.

## 31. Journey Automation： How to Optimize the Full Customer Journey

Let's be honest, most of us are just
scratching the surface of our marketing
automation. You probably sent out a few
emails, filled out a couple property
values, and called it a day. But what if

disconnected moments. They go through an

create. To follow along with everything
I'm about to show you, click the link in
the description down below. I'm Thomas.
This is How to HubSpot.
First, let's understand what we're
building. A customer journey map is a
visual story of how customers interact
with your business from discovering it
all the way through to becoming a loyal
customer and beyond. So, why do customer
journeys matter? Three big reasons. One,
they align your entire team around one
customer narrative. Two, they highlight
what's working points of force and
what's not working points of friction.
And three, they bring your customer-f
facing teams together to make
improvements. When teams don't
communicate well, customers feel it.
Your marketing team might be promising
something that sales doesn't know about,
or your support team might be unaware of
what was sold. Journey mapping prevents
all of these from happening. Okay,
before we jump in, one quick tip. Make
sure that you create at least one buyer
persona so we know who we are mapping
this journey for. To get started, you'll

a

## 34. Optimize Your Website for Increased Conversions

Your website does a lot of different
jobs, but maybe the most important one
is converting visitors into contacts. If
you want to take your conversion rate to

you. I'm Kyle and this is How to
HubSpot.

approach conversion rate optimization.

in. If you want to follow along, click
the link in the description below.
First, let's talk about your homepage.
Your homepage is the most important page
on your website. It's a lot of people's
first impression of your company, and
it'll be the entry point for a lot of
new and returning visitors. You want to
provide the information they're looking
for and draw them in to spending more
time on your site. One example of a
great homepage is Evernote. If you go to
evernote.com, you'll land on this page
here. Right at the top, we've got a
value proposition and a big call to
action. I can get started for free if I
know that's what I want to do. But what
if I'm not sure what Evernote is or I'm
not sure it's right for my needs? Let's
scroll down and see if it helps answer
some of my questions. So, if I scroll
down, right away, I'm given all these
cards that give me an idea of some of
the things Evernote can be used to
create. And down a little bit more, it
tells me more features that I might be
interested in. If I'm still not
convinced that it's a good product, down
here, we get some social proof. Social
proof is an incredibly powerful thing to
share on your homepage. Now, you may not
have been mentioned in some of the
bigname publications that Evernote has,
but perhaps you have customer
testimonials you can share, or maybe you
have some statistics about how you have
helped your customers. Providing this
can give people more confidence in
trying out your products. Another thing
I really like about this page is this
start for free button has been following
me around as I've been scrolling. it's
clear that that is the conversion point
Evernote wants to send me to on your
homepage. Make sure you have one clear
action you want people to take so they
can deepen their engagement with your
company. So, those are some of the
things that makes Evernote's homepage a
great example of how to optimize for
conversions. If you want to build a
homepage that's optimized for
conversions, HubSpot has a whole
marketplace of website templates you can
get started with. No design experience
required. Next up is landing pages.
While converting visitors into customers
is just one of many jobs your homepage
has, your landing pages should be laser
focused on conversion. Let's take a look
at an example of a conversion optimized
landing page. Here's a landing page on
the Netflix website. Notice how simple
this page is. There's a little bit of
information about the value Netflix
offers and how much it costs to get
started. And all they ask for is an
email address. Now, depending on the
product you offer, you may need to
collect more information than just an
email address. But it's always a good
idea to keep your forms as short as
possible. The more information you ask
for, the more people you're going to
lose. So, ask for just the minimal
information you need. Provide a little
bit of information so people know what
they're signing up for, and make it as
simple as possible for people to take
the action you want them to take. Now,
let's talk about pop-ups. Pop-ups got a
bad rap in the early days of the
internet because they were obtrusive,
obnoxious, and literally everywhere. But
the truth is, a well-placed popup can
drive a lot of conversions. And HubSpot
has a great CTAs tool that can help you
with that. Let's take a look. This is
the CTAs tool inside HubSpot. It's under
marketing and CTAs. To create a new CTA,
we'll just come up to the top right
corner and click create. HubSpot has a
big template library with a bunch of
CTAs to help you get started. Notice
that we have banners that appear at the
top of the page, slideins that come into
the corner and actual popups that appear
right in the middle. I'll choose this
template right here so we can build a
pop-up. On this first screen, you're
given a lot of options for design and
you can adjust your messaging. But
what's more relevant for this discussion
are targeting and options. Under the
targeting tab, you can control when this
pop-up will be shown. And the first
option is to trigger on a button click.
I want you to think about that. If you
have a button on your homepage or
anywhere else on your website that sends
someone to a form, you could link them
out to a separate landing page, or you
could have that form show up in a popup
right on the page they're on. They can
then fill in their information and
submit the form and go right back to
browsing where they left off. That's
actually a less interruptive experience
than other alternatives. In this way, a
pop-up can improve the user experience
on your page. Additional options here
include triggering the pop-up on page
scroll and exit intent. For page scroll,
if you toggle this on, you select a
percentage and when they get that far
down on the page, the pop-up will
appear. If you trigger on exit intent,
the pop-up will appear when they leave
the page. So, if you've ever been on a
web page and you moved your mouse to hit
the back button and a pop-up appeared,
that's exit intent. You can also trigger
the pop-up after they've been on the
page a certain number of seconds or
after they've been inactive a certain
number of seconds. So, if they've fallen
asleep, you can wake them up with a
pop-up. The next set of options are for
where this popup will be shown. Do you
want it to show on every page of your
website or just certain ones? You can
get really strategic about that.
Additionally, because HubSpot is one big
interconnected system built on top of
CRM data, you can filter contacts based
on what's stored in your CRM to
determine whether or not they should see
the pop-up. And finally, you can choose
how often this pop-up will be shown. If
you've already shown the pop-up to
someone once, you might not want to
bother them with it again. So, you can
delay it for a certain number of
minutes, days, weeks, months, or even
years. In the options tab, you can turn
off this popup for small screen sizes.
Don't forget about your mobile visitors.
Everybody's on their phones, and if you
have a big popup on a small screen,
that's a bad experience. As you think
about conversion rate optimization,
optimize your website for mobile so you
don't lose those visitors. Don't let
these options overwhelm you. Remember,
the more intentional you are about when
and where your pop-ups appear, the
better they're likely to perform. So,
put some thought into your conversion
strategy and build a pop-up that
reflects it. The last topic I want to
talk about here is page speed. Long
loading times hurt the user experience
and increase bounce rate. And Google
penalizes slow loading web pages. So
even if people are willing to wait
around for your pages to load, you'll be
getting less traffic in the first place.
We don't know yet if page speed affects
AI powered search engines like chat GBT
or Perplexity. But if those sites are
sending people to your web pages and if
those pages are taking a long time to
load, it's likely people will bounce and
go somewhere else. Page speed is a much
more technical topic than the ones we've
talked about so far. So, if you have
someone dedicated to the technical
aspects of your website, you should
bring this up with them. But regardless
of how technical you are, there are
things you can do to improve your
loading times. Generally speaking,
fixing a slow loading web page includes
things like removing and compressing
media files, reducing the number of
themes and plugins used on your site,
removing redirects, and streamlining the
coding and serverside scripts used on
your pages. Additionally, if you use
HubSpot to build your website, you'll
get SEO recommendations for each one of
your web pages. Review those regularly
to look for opportunities to improve
page performance. So, those are my tips
for improving your website's conversion
rate. But before you hop in and start
making changes, you should figure out
what your current conversion rate is. A
good way to do this is take the current
number of conversions for a page during
a set period of time and dividing it by
the total number of visitors to that
page for the same period of time.
That'll give you a percentage. You can
calculate this for an individual page or
your website as a whole. But either way,
as you start making changes, keep an eye
on that number. Okay, so that's a ton of
information about conversion rate
optimization. Remember, your homepage is
the most important page on your website,
but your landing pages and pop-ups are
the parts that are solely focused on
conversion. Start with your homepage,
then move to your landing page, then
start adding in pop-ups where they make
sense. After that, take a look at your
mobile experience and page speeds and
see what you can do to make improvements
there. Throughout it all, measure your
conversion rate and look for it to go
up. If you want to try this for
yourself, click the link in the
description below. I'm Kyle and this is
How to HubSpot. See you on the next one.

## 35. Prospecting Agent： Deeper research and personalized emails at scale

Your reps are drowning in research.
Every prospect needs context. Every
email needs personalization. There just
aren't enough hours in the day to do
it right at scale. Prospecting
agent handles the research and writes
personalized outreach so your team can
focus on the conversations that actually
close deals. Since launch, you've told
us what needed improvement, and we
listened. In this video, I'm
going to show you smarter research,
flexible configuration, truly
personalized emails, and seamless
integration with your existing
workflows. I'm Kyle, and this is how to
HubSpot.
Good prospecting starts with good
research, but manual research kills
momentum. Let me show you how we've
automated the heavy lifting. Prospecting
agent doesn't just send emails. It
researches every single prospect before
writing a word. Here's what the agent
does automatically. It scans the
prospect's company website. It pulls
recent news and announcements. It
reviews your CRM history with that
contact. And it gathers relevant web
data about their industry. Then it uses
all of that context to inform the
outreach. The result, reps save up to
95% of the time they used to spend
digging for context. That research now
happens automatically at scale for every
single prospect. To see this in action,
navigate to prospecting agent in your
sales hub. Click on any active prospect
in a campaign. Look at the research
summary panel and you'll see all the
context agent gathered about this
prospect. The agent did in seconds what
would take your rep 30 minutes or more.
Different segments need different
messages. A product launch email
shouldn't sound like a renewal pitch.
Let me show you how to tailor outreach
without starting from scratch every
time. Selling profiles are the secret to
consistent onbrand outreach at scale.
Here's what a selling profile includes.
Your value proposition, tone and style
guidelines,
preferred call to action, target segment
or use case, and custom instructions for
specific email guidance. You can create
multiple profiles for different
scenarios, product launches, new
verticals, specific personas, or
seasonal campaigns. Here's how to create
one. Go to agent setup.
Click create new selling profile.
Give it a name like enterprise outreach.
Add in your website or product page to
have it pull relevant info about your
offering, value proposition, and more.
Click next. Select an identity. This
controls what email the prospecting
agent will send from.
Click next. Now choose your desired call
to action. Whether that's booking a
meeting, sending a document, or sending
a URL. Click next. You can choose
whether emails need to be reviewed
before sending or they'll send
automatically. And you can also choose a
tone for your agent or use your
company's brand voice. Click next. When
you're ready, click create selling
profile. Your selling profile is now
ready to go. If you click into the
selling profile, you can change any of
the options you set, and you can also
control advanced options, including
turning on custom instructions. Custom
instructions let you coach the agent in
plain English. You might write, "Always
reference recent company news from the
past 30 days." Or, "Keep emails under
100 words." Or for executives, only
reach out when we see a funding or
growth signal or never mention
competitor names directly. When you're
satisfied with your custom instructions,
click save changes.
Now when you create a new prospecting
campaign, you can select this profile.
Your reps get consistent on brand
outreach without rewriting everything
manually. Launching a new product,
targeting a new vertical, testing a new
message. Now you can build a profile for
each use case with specific instructions
tailored to each. Each one stores your
messaging so you're not reinventing the
wheel every time. Generic mail merge
emails get ignored. True
personalization, the kind that gets

scale when humans go at it alone. Let me

that actually sound like someone did the

signals, re-resarching and rewriting

pre-written templates on a timer. Here's

messages. Smart follow-up timing. It
watches engagement signals and adjusts
follow-up timing accordingly, not just
arbitrary 3-day or 7-day intervals. More
than 200 languages supported. Your
global team can prospect anywhere with
native language outreach. The result,
higher response rates, more leads
converted, no extra headcount needed.
Let me show you what a personalized
email looks like. Go to prospecting
agent. Click on a contact in an active
campaign.
Look at the email preview.
Notice how the agent mentions specific
company details, recent news, or
relevant context. This isn't a template
with a firstname token. This is real
personalization grounded in research.
The agent also handles follow-ups
automatically. If a prospect opens but
doesn't reply, it sends a relevant
follow-up. If they click a link, it
adjusts the next message based on what
they engaged with. If they don't engage
at all, it tries a different angle.
Every follow-up is informed by actual
behavior, not guesswork. Prospecting
isn't just cold outbound. It's inbound

acceleration. Let me show you how
prospecting agent works wherever your
leads come from. You can trigger
prospecting agent outreach from any
HubSpot workflow or enroll contacts

Set the enrollment trigger form
submission equals demo request form.
Add an action. Enroll in prospecting
agent campaign. Select your selling

Set any additional parameters, delay,

automatically. Contact downloads a
specific resource? Follow up with
relevant outreach. You can also enroll

integrates with existing sales motions.
Prospecting agent doesn't replace your

contacts at target accounts. Each person

Read a few examples. Make sure the tone

Step four, iterate based on results.

## 40. The Official HubSpot Marketing Hub Tutorial

Hi, I'm Angel. I'm a marketing director
working in tech, and I spent the last
few weeks playing inside of HubSpot's
Marketing Hub. And I'm super super
excited to show you what I learned. This
is how to HubSpot.
Our marketing goals are all the same. We
want to be able to attract more leads,
engage with our customers, personalize
the experience for them, and be able to
track everything all in one place. In
this video, I'm going to show you how
you can do all of that and more inside
of HubSpot's Marketing Hub. By the way,
it's completely free to get started with
HubSpot's Marketing Hub. So, if you want
to follow along, you can check out the
link in the description box below.
Everything to do with marketing always
starts with the customer. That's why the
Marketing Hub is built on top of the
smart CRM system. This is your
centralized customer database where you
can start to understand who's opted in,
who's converted on your forms, and how
long they've been a customer for. This
is also where you can create
segmentations and lists so that you can
get super specific with your marketing
communications. To do that, all you have
to do is go into the side nav under CRM,
click lists,
and then we will create a new list, and
then you'll be able to filter by
specific customer data. HubSpot actually
gives you tons of different ways to
filter, such as by contact, by cart, by
company, by deal. But wait, let's
rewind. How do we actually bring in
these customers? There are a couple of
different tools that you can use. The
first one is forms. So, if you go under
marketing, you can click into forms.
Under forms, you can create embedded
forms, which live on your website
organically, or you can use standalone
pages, which act like landing pages with
forms on them. If you want to create
pop-ups, banners, slide-ins, or embedded
call to actions, you can go to the call
to actions tool, which is right under
the forms tool. Both the forms tool and
the call to action tool gives you tons
of pre-made templates that you can
choose from. What's also really cool
about the call to actions tool is that
it gives you a ton of different
targeting options, which means you can
reach your customer no matter what part
of the customer journey they're in. So,
whether you want to trigger it by button
click, by page scroll, or after an
elapsed time, you have all of those
options there. Once the customers are
in, it's time to turn them into a raving
fans. There's a bunch of different tools
that you can use to do this, so I'm
going to demonstrate a couple so you can
see how easy it is to use. Let's start
with ads, a great way to stay top of
mind with your customers. To find ads,
you can go under the marketing tab and
then the ads tab.
If it's your first time connecting your
ad accounts, HubSpot has a super
easy-to-use step-by-step onboarding
process that will help you through it.
But once you have your ad accounts
connected, you'll be able to see all of
your existing ads as well as their
metrics all in this dashboard. When
you're creating an ad, of course, the
first thing you want to start with is
your audience.
The audiences feature leverages the
customer data that you've collected into
your smart CRM system, letting you
target the customers at different points
of the journey. When you're creating an
audience, you have the options to
segment them via website visitors,
contact list, company list, or even
look-alike audiences.
Once you have your audience, we can
start creating our ad campaign. There
are a bunch of different ad types that
you can choose from, but let's walk
through how to create a search ad. When
you're on this screen, you can decide
whether you want to create a new ad or
add to one of your existing ads. Today,
we're going to go through the new ad.
Just like with all of their other tools,
HubSpot has AI built in so that you
never have to worry about not being able
to think of a headline or description.
To use the AI assistant, you just have
to click the button, type in a prompt
that works for your ad, and then it's
automatically going to generate the
headline as well as the description for
you.
HubSpot actually breaks down all the
different parts of your ad campaign so
that it makes it really easy for you to
set up your settings. So, if you want to
set up your keywords, there is the
keywords tab, the targeting tab makes
sure that you are reaching the right
audience. The budget and schedule tool
makes sure that you are not
overspending, and they have an
automations tab which allows you to
decide what you want to do after your ad
campaign. So, once your customers have
converted or have engaged with your ad,
you can send them an email or even tag
them into an audience. When your ads are
up and running, it's time to analyze
them with the analyze tab. The analyze
tab gives you a really great overview on
how your ads are doing as a whole.
Because we don't have any live ads
running right now, a lot of the numbers
are going to show up as zeros. However,
I still wanted to show you how the
dashboard is going to provide all of the
key metrics such as your impressions,
clicks, and ad spend.

in general, selling has never been as
